The Message


It has taken far too long, but I now finally realize the following - people want to hear certain things from certain people. I know - shocking, right? People want to hear what they want to hear. And anything that is opposed to that makes them grumble. So rather than always deal with the griping of in-person conversation concerning such seemingly controversial topics such as God and life and death, I've decided to create this website. For the beauty in this is that you read what I write if you want to or are curious about what I've said and for no other reason. No one is forcing you to read thus far, and that's a wonderful and beautiful thing. If you want to go and do something else and forget about everything I've said on here, you totally can, and you totally should if that's how you genuinely feel.

But if there's a part of you that is curious about questioning the nature of things around you, I urge you to read on, with the upmost yearning for joy and for life and for this moment, because I promise you - there is a level of connection out there that is so beautiful I want everyone to have it even if it kills me.

Beauty

There is so much beauty in the world. If you blink, you'll miss it.

Yep.

I’ll say it before, and I’ll say it again. Life moves pretty fast. You don’t stop and look around once and awhile, you could miss it.

You don’t stop and give a real good look at the brevity of existence, the vanity of human pursuit, and yet the simultaneous and inescapable beauty of life – you will miss it.

It's like my whole life I have been stumbling, fumbling to articulate these words which are before you now.

This is as delicately as I can put it.

I've done quite a bit of thinking and as of now I have quite a bit to say…

Long has my soul been wanting to communicate this message to anyone and everyone, and now that I have the time, the perspective, the words, and the will, I finally may do so.

What I have sought out of life is how to live it in full.

My credentials are my credentials. You will either like what I have to say or you will not. So do not let any externalities influence your judgment on my message. Judge the message. And if you find the message to be sound and of good nature, then you know you can trust the messenger.

I have sought to ponder the complexities of the universe and likewise the human spirit and I have loved every firing of every neuron.

Let me level with you, like a man.

I was sent here to tell you the most wonderful news - and I fear that if you blink, you may miss it.



PART 1 - A NECESSARY PRECURSOR


"I'd tell you all you want and more, if the sounds I made could be what you hear."

- David Foster Wallace, Infinite Jest


If you are searching for a sign, this is it.

If you are reading this, it's not too late.


"We have, each of us, a life-story, an inner narrative - whose continuity, whose sense, is our lives. It might be said that each of us constructs and lives, a 'narrative', and that this narrative is us, our identities. If we wish to know about a man, we ask 'what is his story - his real, inmost story?' - for each of us is a biography, a story. Each of us is a singular narrative, which is constructed, continually, unconsciously, by, through, and in us - through our perceptions, our feelings, our thoughts, our actions; and, not least, our discourse, our spoken narrations. Biologically, physiologically, we are not so different from each other; historically, as narratives - we are each of us unique. To be ourselves we must have ourselves - possess, if need be re-possess, our life stories. We must 'recollect' ourselves, recollect the inner drama, the narrative, of ourselves. A man needs such a narrative, a continuous inner narrative, to maintain his identity, his self."

- Oliver Sacks, The Man Who Mistook His Wife For A Hat


Life is precious.

Life is all about relationships. It is about the moments you share with the people beside you.

In order to have a relationship, you must sacrifice something – whether it be time, opportunity, or your very own life. A relationship, at the very least, is made up of two distinct entities that choose to engage with each other because it is mutually beneficial to do so.

Ask anyone that has been in the trenches of a relationship and they will tell you what a successful relationship really all boils down to – communication.

What is communication?

Communication is the absolute most important component to a thriving and mutually beneficial relationship. Why is this true? Because communication breeds understanding and genuine understanding within a relationship leads to a significant and better experience for everyone involved. Communication reinforces the bonds within a relationship, which is necessary to sustain it.

To communicate is to pass on information.

To make matters simpler, let us call one entity in a relationship the giver, when they are the ones giving information and let us call the other entity in the relationship the receiver, when they are the ones receiving the information.

So, in a relationship where communication occurs, the giver passes on information to the receiver. This then increases the knowledge of the receiver of the information, ideally leading to a wiser and better suited response from the receiver, all to the benefits of all parties involved.

Why do we communicate?

In a functioning relationship, both sides communicate with each other. One side gives a message which the other side receives. Then, the roles are reversed, and the one who received now gives, and the one who gave now receives. On and on and on, all to the benefit of both sides in a healthy and righteous relationship. This is how a relationship works.

This is the gift of life - to be able to engage in relationships and interactions and encounters with one another, to be able to share great moments of all kinds.

And that’s the funny thing about this world that we currently share – if you are human and you have the breath of life in you, you crave a certain kind of connection with whoever is around you. You crave to be known by others and to know others. You crave to be loved by others and to love others. You crave to be wanted by others and to want others. You crave to experience others and have others experience you.

And that is why we communicate – to be known and to know, to be loved and to love, to be wanted and to want, and to be experienced and to experience.

And that too is what we desire out of life – to be known and to know, to be loved and to love, to be wanted and to want, and to be experienced and to experience. To give and receive.

It is put more eloquently in Children of the Mind by Orson Scott Card: "No, she doesn't want that. Not in her deepest heart. She wants what everyone wants - to be loved and cared for, to be part of something beautiful and fine, to have the respect of those she admires."

I firmly believe, on some level, all individuals want the above. Even those that would swear otherwise. We all want to have good experiences, and if we cannot find the love that our soul craves, or be part of something that is beautiful and fine, or garner the respect from esteemed individuals, then we search for those feelings elsewhere, often times at the expense of overtly vain and selfish pursuits.

Here is what I want to reiterate at this point:

  1. Life is about relationships.
  2. Communication is what makes or breaks a relationship.

We all experience life (and relationships in life (and communication within relationships in life)) hoping for what is really the same thing - something (or perhaps, someone) that provides the love that we truly crave, the wisdom that we truly desire, and the relationship fulfillment which we all yearn for.

In fact, something cannot provide the love we truly crave, because it takes a person (or some intelligent identity) to actually, verbally, actively love.

Something cannot provide the wisdom that we truly desire, because in order to imitate true wisdom, there needs to be a personal example in one's life. You need to see and know a wise person to properly understand wisdom.

Something cannot fulfill us from a relational standpoint, because there is no real relationship between an individual and something. The individual may give information and the individual may receive information - but the object, the thing - no matter how much it imitates identity - cannot genuinely give information and receive information - at least not to the extent another human being may.

No, life is about genuine and authentic relationships between people. No screen, no virtual reality, no artificial intelligence, no inauthentic experience of reality will satiate our palate for fulfilling relationships, but face-to-face honest communication between individuals. Life is about meeting amazing people and cultivating authentic and wonderful relationships with the people around you. But that’s not it, either. This paragraph is close to what it’s all about, but it is not it entirely.

Life is about the someone. Life is about the someone that can and will provide the love we truly crave, the wisdom we truly desire, and the relationship fulfillment we all yearn for. Because if you know what it means to be human, then you know, to your core, no doubt, that to be human is to love imperfectly, to frolic in folly and hypocrisy and sin, and to demand a certain selflessness in others that you fail to provide yourself. So, in this world, it is not enough to know and be known, to love and be loved, to want and be wanted, to experience and be experienced by the imperfection of others because we are designed to be fulfilled by the perfection of the ultimate epitome of relationship – the relationship between oneself and the Lord God Almighty.

But I'm getting ahead of myself.

First things first.

So there is life. And life is a series of relationships. And the quality of relationships are increased through communication.

And so to what end do we all go through life communicating often with many people?

Bearing in mind that we all want basically the same thing – to know and to be known, to love and to be loved, to want and to be wanted, and to experience and be experienced – why is there so much corruption, hatred, murder, slander, gossip, misunderstanding, brokenness, fraud, illness, depression, jealousy and pure sheer evil in this world of ours?

By and large, people have goodness in their heart and people will do good things if called upon, if they understand it is worthwhile to do the good thing. But here's an issue in this world of man: no one asks, no one reaches out, no one takes just and righteous advantage of their peers and the world around them. Something halts us from great communication and the ability to follow through on trusting others.

And that something is fear. Because communicating intimately with someone requires a certain vulnerability that we all are typically only comfortable sharing with a husband or a wife, and tragically, often times not even then.

But what if it was possible to not let that fear build up walls your ego guards day and night? What if it was possible to let love tear down those walls that, while deceptively claiming to be keeping you safe from the outside world, are in reality keeping the outside world from seeing your honest self who is truly brilliant, especially when understood completely?

But that's a question for those born again, those who produce LIFE by the power of the ULTIMATE LIFE-GIVER.

And we are all born busy in death. But the beautiful thing is – we get to decide. We have the power to choose. Death or life. Ourselves or others. Selfishness or selflessness. Hate of rivals or love for enemies. Stubbornness or forgiveness. Wrong or right. Evil or good.

And as I grow older and older and eventually die here on this putrid earth which rots in sin, I can feel my sense of hearing dying too. And that depresses me greatly, because music is a wonderful thing. But, though the cacophony and confusion of reality produces a lot of noise in the ears of a person inclined to hear, it all remains gorgeously melodious music because I know the someone who can and will and did and does provide the richest love in all of existence, the someone who genuinely wants to engage in authentic relationship with every single human being, the someone who not only wants to know and be known, to love and be loved, to want and be wanted, to experience and be experienced - but is the catalyst and overseer and LORD of every relationship ever. AND BECAUSE OF HIM - BECAUSE OF THE LORD GOD - BEAUTY ABOUNDS, LOVE SPREADS, GRACE SURVIVES, PEOPLE LIVE, AND THE WHEEL OF HISTORY CONTINUES TO ROLL DOWN HIS PATH OF MYSTERIOUS GLORY.

And so, I now reveal to you what this website is.

This is a call to those who are alive. The phone is ringing, my friend. Pick up! There's someone at the door. Go open it!

And to those who are dead or dying - this is my serenade, my song, my heart-throbbing, gut-wrenching, last-ditch cry for you to die to deathly and lawless ways, to see self-seeking for the chaotic vanity that it is, and ultimately to be disciplined in righteousness and repentance through an undying trust in the righteousness of the Lord God.

And repentance is nothing more than choosing to turn away from worshipping and loving sin to, instead, like you are designed, so as to maximize the joy and love of who you are, and for the sake of your well-being, to focus all of your heart and mind and soul on loving and knowing and wanting and experiencing the Lord God, whose character and being can be found in the personhood of Jesus Christ, who lived a perfect life and then died on a cross, crucified by His people who misunderstood Him and His Word, and then three days later was resurrected from the grave, and is now seated at the right hand of Our Heavenly Father, who rules heaven and earth and has power over all, who loves His people so dearly and with such compassion that He gave His only son so that they may be with Him despite their sinful self-absorption.




PART 2 - INTRODUCTION

Life is characterized by movement of its own accord.


This means to be alive


one must be in motion,


one must be changing.


Life is characterized by this ability to change.


This means


if you are stagnant in your growth,


if you are incapable of changing,


you are as good as dead.


So to live righteously is to recognize the good and evil within you, to die to that evil and to strive for the good, and change. And then love others with the veracity of Jesus Christ.

Psalm 103:

Of David

Bless the Lord, O my soul: and all that is within me, bless his holy name.

Who forgiveth all thine iniquities; who healeth all thy diseases;

Who redeemeth thy life from destruction; who crowneth thee with lovingkindness and tender mercies;

Who satisfieth thy mouth with good things; so that thy youth is renewed like the eagle's.

The Lord executeth righteousness and judgment for all that are oppressed.

He made known his ways unto Moses, his acts unto the children of Israel.

The Lord is merciful and gracious, slow to anger, and plenteous in mercy.

He will not always chide: neither will he keep his anger for ever.

He hath not dealt with us after our sins; nor rewarded us according to our iniquities.

For as the heaven is high above the earth, so great is his mercy toward them that fear him.

As far as the east is from the west, so far hath he removed our transgressions from us.

Like as a father pitieth his children, so the Lord pitieth them that fear him.

For he knoweth our frame; he remembereth that we are dust.

As for man, his days are as grass: as a flower of the field, so he flourisheth.

For the wind passeth over it, and it is gone; and the place thereof shall know it no more.

But the mercy of the Lord is from everlasting to everlasting upon them that fear him, and his righteousness unto children's children;

To such as keep his covenant, and to those that remember his commandments to do them.

The Lord hath prepared his throne in the heavens; and his kingdom ruleth over all.

Bless the Lord, ye his angels, that excel in strength, that do his commandments, hearkening unto the voice of his word.

Bless ye the Lord, all ye his hosts; ye ministers of his, that do his pleasure.

Bless the Lord, all his works in all places of his dominion: bless the Lord, O my soul.


John 5:24-47

Verily, verily, I say unto you, He that hearteh my word, and believeth on him that sent me, hath everlasting life, and shall not come into dondemnation; but is passed from death unto life.

Verily, verily, I say unto you, The hour is coming, and now is, when the dead shall hear the voice of the Son of God: and they that hear shall live.

For as the Father hath life in himself; so hath he given to the Son to have life in himself;

And hath given him authority to execute judgment also, because he is the Son of man.

Marven not at this: for the hour is coming, in the which all that are in the graves shall hear his voice,

And shall come forth; they that have done good, unto the resurrection of life; and they that have done evil, unto the resurrection of damnation.

I can of mine own self do nothing: as I hear, I judge: and my judgment is just; because I seek not mine own will, but the will of the Father which hath sent me.

If I bear witness of myself, my witness is not true.

There is another that beareth witness of me; and I know that the witness whcih he witnesseth of me is true.

Ye sent unto John, and he bare witness unto the truth.

But I receive not testimony from man: but these things I say, that ye might be saved.

He was a burning and a shining light: and ye were willing for a season to rejoice in his light.

But I have greater witness than that of John: for the works which the Father hath given me to finish, the same works that I do, bear witness of me, that the Father hath sent me.

And the Father himself, which hath sent me, hath borne witness of me. Ye have neither heard his voice at any time, nor seen his shape.

And ye have not his word abiding in you: for whom he hath sent, him ye believe not.

Search the scriptures; for in them ye think ye have eternal life: and they are they which testify of me.

And ye will not come to me, that ye might have life.

I receive not honour from men.

But I know you, that ye have not the love of God in you.

I am come in my Father's name, and ye receive me not: if another shall come in his own name, him ye will receive.

How can ye believe, which receive honour one of another, and seek not the honour that cometh from God only?

Do not think that I will accuse you to the Father: there is one that accuseth you, even Moses, in whom ye trust.

For had ye believed Moses, ye would have believed me: for he wrote of me.

But if ye believe not his writings, how shall ye believe my words?

A good chunk of the first part of this website will be explaining what I’m trying to get at with all these words. There are many things that I want you to understand through this message.

Here are some links to some great videos. Hopefully, these compliment the sort of natural seriousness that surfaces when discussing the matters that I wish to bring to light.

What I mean to tell you requires, for lack of a better word, a certain degree of maturity. And too often we think that maturity requires no sense of humor.

Whose Line Is It Anyway?

Everything

I have found what Rob Bell says here to be spot on – what you look for, you will find.

What are you looking for?

What I have sought after in life can be summed up in the following questions:

  1. What is good? And what are the fruits of being good?
  2. What is evil? And what are the fruits of being evil?
  3. What is love? And what are the fruits of loving?
  4. What is hate? And what are the fruits of hating?
  5. What is selflessness? And what are the fruits of being selfless?
  6. What is selfishness? And what are the fruits of being selfish?
  7. How may I live life to the fullest?
  8. What physical, social, intellectual, and personal pleasures are most fulfilling?
  9. What is wisdom and how does one live a wise life?
  10. How may I make the most out of my time here?
  11. How may I be a blessing to everyone I meet?
  12. How do I find true joy?
  13. Why are we here?
  14. What is my purpose?
  15. Why is there so much disconnection between people in the world?
  16. What ought I to fear and what ought I to love?

My whole life I have yearned to stretch my eyes open to this underlying beauty which pervades our reality that can only be described as “the divine”. I have found it is not of one's own will that their eyes are opened to this all-encompassing beauty, but the sole doing of Our Heavenly Father. And per His will, I have found that we and likewise our surroundings are absolutely drenched in it.

I refuse to live a life where I am not fully present. It has taken longer than I would have liked, but I have learned and am still learning how to be in love with the present moment. My fear is that many, like myself in the past, and no doubt on occasion in my future, will miss the moment. This is terrifying upon reflection, because when all is said and done, and we are able to look past our anxieties and fears concerning our troublesome past or our unknown future, the present moment is the only thing we really have.

From the poem of creation to the weirdness of the universe on both a large and small scale, to dimensions and understanding, to the combination and clashing of the physical self versus the spiritual self within the human being, I have long been left speechless before the beauty surrounding me.

But now I have something to say. And I'll be saying it until the day I die.

THERE. IS. MORE.

To you. To life. To your role in life. To everything. There is so much going on here, on this earth.

I am so utterly convinced of it that I have dropped out of college and gone overseas to give my whole self over to the discovery and exploration of experiencing the hidden but deep beauty of life.

I had to leave conventional education because, in school – at least in my own circumstances, I was quickly learning to distract myself with the mundane as well as from honestly comprehending the majesty of existence and the beauty of sacred personalities around me. (And that, my friends, is all that matters. Forget that and you are a dead man walking.) I was overly busy with what I realized were ultimately meaningless pursuits, because eventually I understood that all of the many hoops people jump through to perform a certain way in school are - unless it truly is your absolute dream to have a certain occupation that requires particular schooling - in order to make more money...and money, while necessary, is, unless properly tamed, an extremely evil idol to the soul. Likewise, the deceptive culture of prosperity, materialism, and, more than anything - hedonism, which has all been carefully and sinisterly cultivated in American society has succeeded in the hearts and minds of many to, unbeknownst to them that covet that life, their detriment. Additionally, especially knowing what I know now concerning the truth and Jesus Christ, when you step back and see how universities (except for a select few) are blatantly biased against anything that isn't in line with the liberal agenda (whose advocates are desperate to try to create and promote their own righteousness outside of the only place where righteousness comes from - that given by the Judeo-Christian God), how there are literally MAJORS now called "Gender Studies" and "Evolutionary Biology", how way too much money is charged for information that could be found elsewhere for free (admittedly though, people go to college for the experience and resources and resume-building, not so much for learning the actual information), you see how college is another deep breeding ground for indoctrination into accepting the tenets, lifestyle, and operation of the new world order, and at the very least numbs people to the evil within the world, teaching all sorts of falsehood because it neglects the reason for life (because people can't accept the true reason - Jesus Christ - because we love to be the god of our own lives, thinking we are the god of our future, and the god of what is good for people to do...but our life only becomes genuinely alive when we make Jesus Christ the righteous God of it, for He knows the future, and He alone knows what is truly good for people to do). I also began to understand how it is especially fruitless to find pride and self-esteem in any secular work - except insofar as your job allows you to connect others to Jesus - because the end result of all human achievement on this present earth is going to be the evil new world order that the Bible exposes. And then you realize people's eternity, people's soul, is what is truly at stake here, and one's bank account and silly piece of paper listing worldly accomplishments in order to persuade others to increase one's bank account suddenly becomes a cruel joke compared to the value of another human being...

I will refuse to let the world kill me and my spirit.

And so here is what the Lord did to me to get me to be where I am now.

The Lord gave me a taste of a fraction of true naked vanity - the state of our heart when we are not in tune with His composition. And what I perceived was horrifying.

I created this website in order to better illustrate to any who are curious enough what I know to be true to the core of my soul – one of many things being that life is meant to be lived in full, our potential is meant to be met, love is meant to be cherished, and above all, our relationships with others are to be adored and cultivated with care.

I hope that after watching the above link, in addition to recognizing the bewildering environment surrounding you at the present moment, you may agree you and I live in an awesome and captivating reality.

I have fallen in love – with the awesomeness, that is. And for a long time, I thought it was the awesomeness of this world – despite it being the chaotic mess that it is.

But now it is clear that all of the awesomeness has one powerful source - and He has a name, and a throne, and a soul, and He is carefully cultivating the most amazing kingdom that ever will be.

And right now the invitation is out, and the letter to everyone is the Bible, the Holy Book of God that the world spits on because it calls out the world for what it is - evil and lost.

I know I have reiterated my intentions again and again, but I must be as clear as possible with matters like these. What I’m aiming to accomplish through all of what I’m telling you is to properly and fully explain to you why we should be in consistent awe of life, people, and our potential, because of how great the King of kings is. Now that I have the time to collect my thoughts and the will to spill my soul, I am going to explain to the best of my ability why our duty is to love the truth through our actions and our hearts – and this especially means not doing whatever is right in our own eyes. I am going to explain how we should have no fear of all earthly endeavors that seek to plague our minds with dread, especially when we know that heaven is knocking at our door. And, ultimately, I’m going to answer the question that has plagued my mind my entire life:

What's this all about?




PART 3 - BREAKFAST

First, let us paint a picture of what life is. Go take it easy and watch Pulp Fiction by Quentin Tarantino in full and get back to me. This section will only make complete sense if you have seen the movie recently.

Though a film is a falsely created reality, a series of deliberate illusions, and though the actual narrative of Pulp Fiction is entirely fictional, I believe that Pulp Fiction is packed with so many aspects of reality that it deserves to be understood in full. Now, this film is so amazing because it resonates with reality in a variety of ways that, upon further inquiry, accurately correlate with the world as we know it. I am going to illustrate what these different aspects are and use Pulp Fiction as a platform to define what life is.

If this website is anything, it is the equivalent of Jules Winnfield sitting down with Vincent Vega for breakfast as they discuss the happenings of their world. Both men experienced something. Both men experienced life that morning. One is unaffected by the coincidences around him and the other is deeply moved by the miracles around him. One dismisses life as chance and a series of random movements, indecipherable coincidence. And the other is confident that something higher and greater than themselves is involved, in control, and orchestrating something greater than what we can imagine. I’m here to tell you, go, look around you, go outside to the highest hill in your neighborhood, gaze up into the sky, feel the silent buzz of the atmosphere enveloping you, be keenly aware of the intricacies of your heart and the complexity of your mind and listen as carefully as you can to the words of Mr. Winnfield: “This was divine intervention.”

And odds are you do not have the effort to continue reading - that is, assuming you have punished your time and eyes thus far at all. Or, you do not believe reading what I have to say would be worthwhile. And that is a fine and reasonable conclusion. By all means, return to what you would rather do or what you need to be doing. But, please, for your sake, question the reality around you and truly seek to know if there is indeed more to life than what meets the eye. And if this is where our time together stops, I have to leave you with the only proper response I can think of, courtesy of Jules Winnfield himself: “Don’t do that. Don’t fuckin’ blow this shit off. What happened here was a fuckin’ miracle. This shit doesn’t just happen. We should be fuckin’ dead, my friend. What happened here was a miracle and I want you to fucking acknowledge it.”

***

Right now, I’m Jules, and you and I, we’re out to breakfast. It’s early, and we have a full day ahead of us. The sun is beaming down hot, sweet, succulent sunshine and the diner we’re at is alive with chatter, busy brains, and meandering minds. I am going to let the conversation between the gangster and soon to be ex-gangster ensue as a prelude to what I must tell you concerning Pulp Fiction and life as we know it.

Vincent Vega: “Oh man, that’s good. That’s good, man. You’re, like, starting to lighten up. You’ve been sittin’ there, all serious and shit.”

Jules Winnfield: “Man, I’ve just been sittin’ here thinkin’.”

Vincent Vega: "About what?"

Jules Winnfield: "About the miracle we witnessed."

Vincent Vega: "The miracle you witnessed. I witnessed a freak occurrence."

Jules Winnfield: "What is a miracle, Vincent?"

Vincent Vega: "An act of God."

Jules Winnfield: "And what's an act of God?"

Vincent Vega: "When, um, God makes the impossible possible. But, this morning I don't think qualifies."

Jules Winnfield: “Hey Vincent, don’t you see, that shit don’t matter. Your judgin’ this shit the wrong way. I mean it could be God stopped the bullets, he changed Coke to Pepsi, he found my fuckin’ car keys. You don’t judge shit like this based on merit. Now whether or not what we experienced was an according to Hoyle miracle is insignificant. But what is significant, is I felt the touch of God. God got involved.”

Vincent Vega: "But why?"

Jules Winnfield: “Well, that’s what’s fuckin’ with me, I don’t know why. But I can’t go back to sleep.”

Vincent Vega: "You serious? You really thinkin' about quittin'?"

Jules Winnfield: "The life?"

Vincent Vega: "Yeah."

Jules Winnfield: "Most definitely."

Vincent Vega: "Fuck. Whatcha gonna do then?"

Jules Winnfield: “Well, that’s what I’ve been sitting here, contemplating. First, I’m going to deliver this case to Marsellus. Then, basically, I’m just going to walk the Earth.”

Vincent Vega: "Whatchu mean, "walk the earth"?"

Jules Winnfield: “You know, like Caine in Kung Fu. Walk from place to place…meet people…get in adventures.”

Vincent Vega: "And how long do you intend to walk the earth?"

Jules Winnfield: "Until God puts me where He wants me to be."

Vincent Vega: "And what if He don't do that?"

Jules Winnfield: "Well, if it takes forever, then I'll walk forever."

Vincent Vega: "So you decided to be a bum?"

Jules Winnfield: "I'll just be Jules, Vincent. No more, no less."

Vincent Vega: “No, Jules, you decided to be a bum. Just like all those pieces of shit out there that beg for change, who sleep in garbage bins, who eat what I throw away. They got a name for that, Jules. It’s called a bum. And without a job, a residence, or legal tender, that’s what you’re gonna be man – a fuckin’ bum.”

Jules Winnfield: "Look, my friend, this is just where you and I differ."

Vincent Vega: "Jules, look, what happened this morning, man, I agree, it was peculiar, but water into wine, I -"

Jules Winnfield: "All shapes and sizes, Vincent."

Vincent Vega: "Don't fuckin' talk to me that way, man."

Jules Winnfield: "If my answers frighten you, Vincent, then you should cease asking scary questions."

Vincent Vega: “I’m gonna take a shit…Let me ask you somethin’. When did you make this decision, when you were sittin’ there eatin’ that muffin’?”

Jules Winnfield: “Well yeah. I was sittin’ here eatin’ my muffin and drinkin’ my coffee, replayin’ the incident in my head, when I had, what alcoholics refer to as “a moment of clarity”.”

Vincent Vega: "Fuck. To be continued."

This is the situation that I am presented with. I am like Jules in that I have felt the touch of God. God got involved. And the world is like Vincent in that it does not understand Jules and it absolutely does not know nor understand the God that has been involved in Jules’ whole life.

This is a God who is involved in all of our lives, whether we know it or not. This is a God of love, a God that seeks a relationship with you, yes, YOU READING THIS. The Great Creator, the Righteous Judge, the Sovereign King, the Ruling-Center-of-All-That-Is, the Great-I-Am loves you more than you can imagine. The problem is, in order for love in a relationship to be realized, both parties have to want to engage with each other. And so God will never force you to do anything with Him. He will let you do as you see fit, if you so wish. (How amazing is that? The freedom He gives us...) But doing as you see fit outside of a relationship with God will only lead to despair in the long run (whether in this life or the next), because all that is good comes from the Lord - every gift of every kind. But I am, and many others are, here to tell you that a relationship with God is what is lacking in all of us. And God has revealed himself through his only begotten Son, Jesus Christ.

I began seeking God not too long ago and now that I see sin for what it is, and truth for what it is, I see God was and is and will be with me always. And I haven’t uncovered anywhere close to half of all the wonder and joy and glory of life, but I know that I am onto something that is absolutely and amazingly good. And I know that the love that I am near to is what we all long for at the core of our being – the love and relationship and fulfillment provided by Jesus Christ. Many hate Jesus Christ and therefore love death (because Jesus Christ is who brings forth life...), but I know that if everyone could see Jesus for who he is, and come to know Him for who he is, they would realize that He is what they have been seeking in everything. He is the solution to all of our problems. He is the answer to all of our questions. He is the author of all the brilliance that you are blessed to know.

Hear me out on all that I have to say and I believe it will have been well worth your time.

Back to what life is.

Here is the argument I am making. Pulp Fiction is like life and life is like Pulp Fiction. Here's why.

  1. Life is a story, just like how Pulp Fiction is a story.

    A story is a narrative designed to interest, amuse, or instruct the reader or listener. A narrative is an account or series of events or experiences. In other words, a story is a series of experiences meant to grip the attention of the person experiencing the story. A story has a beginning and an end, and a middle full of conflict. Whether you agree or not, you have a beginning and an end, and a middle that is full of ups and downs and highs and lows and good times and bad times. A story has a protagonist, a primary character that it follows. You are the protagonist of your story, and you interact regularly with secondary characters that have influence on your day and what you do in it. Conversely, you play the role of a secondary character in the lives of many other people, some more than others.

    In Pulp Fiction, there are six relatively main characters. Now each of those individual characters follow their own narrative arc. Some overlap, some don’t. So it is with our lives. We all are the main character of our own life. We all are the center of our own world. We all are walking and talking stories.

  2. Life as we know it now on earth is bloody and vulgar and brutal, just like the happenings of Pulp Fiction.

    The word “fuck” is used 265 times. With 154 minutes of film, that’s an average of 1.7 uses of the word "fuck" a minute. Perhaps we are not all so vulgar in our own lives, but at the very least we all experience things that hold the capacity to frustrate us to a crude degree.

    Need I remind us of the brutal sexual violence against Marsellus Wallace, or car wreck, triple homicide, uzi-murder, overdose, restaurant hostage situation that takes place throughout the film? Life is this brutal to people. It’s utter mayhem out there. And on some level, everything humans do are attempts at distractions that ease this force of brute reality. No one can handle it alone, and so we all turn to either something or someone to relinquish our pain and suffering – whether it be some form of a drug, career, entertainment, a significant other, family, or a higher power...little do we know though that only one thing will completely and forever relinquish our pain and suffering - and that is Jesus Christ, what He did for us on the cross, and what He does for us now.

    We are all on this coarse river of life, and you can either learn how to fight the rapids the right way – with true effectiveness by the doing of Jesus Christ, or drown of exhaustion in the end – consumed by the chaos of the waves. Don't keep relying on fallible people in your life and unhelpful pursuits and objects - come to Jesus, and He will relinquish your pain and suffering forever - but you have to let Him...

  3. Life will never go as you expect it, just like it went for the characters in Pulp Fiction.

    There are essentially six primary characters that are followed throughout Pulp Fiction. Pumpkin and Honey Bunny, Mia Wallace, Vincent Vega, Jules Winnfield, and Butch Coolidge. Bearing in mind that having unexpected things happen to your characters is also just a mark of good storytelling (because then your story resembles reality!), here are some good examples.

    1. Pumpkin and Honey Bunny are the two misfits aiming to get money by robbing a place. Here is some dialogue from the first scene of the movie.

      Pumpkin: “Nobody ever robs restaurants. Bars. Liquor stores. Gas stations. You get your head blown off stickin it in one of them. Restaurants, on the other hand, you catch them with their pants down. They’re not expecting to get robbed. Not as expecting, anyway.”

      Honey Bunny: “I bet you could cut down on the hero factor in a place like this.”

      Pumpkin: “Correct. Same as banks, these places are insured. Manager, he don’t give a fuck, he just tryin’ to get you out the door before you start pluggin’ the diners. Waitresses, fuckin’ forget it. No way they’re takin’ a bullet for the register. Bus boys, some wetbag gettin’ paid a dollar fifty an hour, really give a fuck you’re stealin’ from the owner. Customers sittin’ there with food in their mouths, they don’t know what’s goin’ on. One minute, they’re havin’ a Denver omelette, next minute, someone’s stickin’ a gun in their face.”

      Expectation: Pumpkin and Honey Bunny will not encounter any opposition or interference in their attempt to rob the restaurant.

      Reality: They happen to rob a restaurant with experienced gangsters that do oppose and interfere with their operation.


    2. Mia Wallace sits down with Vincent's coat on after a night out with Mr. Vega.

      Expectation: She is going to snort cocaine.

      Reality: She ends up snorting heroin.


    3. Butch Coolidge has just played the fight so that Marsellus Wallace loses, and is ready to escape with Fabienne, retire and live on an island.

      Expectation: Butch's plans to leave work out like he originally planned, and his father's watch is right where it needs to be.

      Reality: Butch has the "singlehandedly strangest day of his life", after having to fetch his watch that Fabienne forgot, killing Vincent Vega, and running into Marsellus Wallace on the street at seeming coincidence.


    4. Vincent Vega takes Mia Wallace out and swears the night will go smoothly.

      Vincent Vega: "What's her name again?"

      Jules Winnfield: "Mia. Why you so interested in big man's wife?"

      Vincent Vega: "Well, Marsellus is leavin' for Florida and when he's gone, he wants me to take care of Mia."

      Jules Winnfield: "Take care of her?"

      Vincent Vega: "Not that! Take her out. Show her a good time. Don't let her get lonely."

      Jules Winnfield: "You're gonna be takin' Mia Wallace out on a date?"

      Vincent Vega: "It ain't a date. It's like when you and your buddy's wife go to a movie or somethin'. It's just...you know...good company."

      Jules just looks at him.

      Vincent Vega: "It's not a date."

      Jules just looks at him.

      Vincent Vega: "I'm not gonna be a bad boy."

      Expectation: Vincent's night out with Mia goes smoothly.

      Reality: Mia overdoses on Vincent's heroin and Vincent has to administer adrenaline to her heart, barely escaping punishment from Marsellus for contributing to the death of his wife.


    5. Jules Winnfield encounters death but escapes alive. The fourth man storms into the room where Jules and Vincent are, expecting that everyone is accounted for.

      Fourth man: "Die...die...die...die...!"

      Peculiarly escaping the bullets, Vincent and Jules kill the fourth man and address the situation at hand.

      Vincent Vega: “Why the fuck didn’t you tell us about that guy in the bathroom? Slip your mind? Forget he was in there with a goddamn hand cannon?”

      Jules Winnfield: “We should be fuckin’ dead right now. Did you see that gun he fired at us? It was bigger than him.”

      Vincent Vega: “.357.”

      Jules Winnfield: “We should be fuckin’ dead!”

      Vincent Vega: “Yeah, we were lucky.”

      Jules Winnfield: “That shit wasn’t luck. That shit was somethin’ else.”

      Vincent Vega: “Yeah, maybe.”

      Jules Winnfield: “That was…divine intervention. You know what divine intervention is?”

      Vincent Vega: “Yeah, I think so. That means God came down from Heaven and stopped the bullets.”

      Jules Winnfield: “Yeah, man, that’s what it means. That’s exactly what it means! God came down from Heaven and stopped the bullets.”

      Vincent Vega: “I think we should be going now.”

      Jules Winnfield: “Don’t do that! Don’t you fuckin’ do that! Don’t blow this shit off! What just happened was a fuckin’ miracle!”

      Vincent Vega: “Chill the fuck out, Jules, this shit happens.”

      Jules Winnfield: “Wrong, wrong, this shit doesn’t just happen.”

      Vincent Vega: “Do you wanna continue this theological discussion in the car, or at the jailhouse with the cops?”

      Jules Winnfield: “We should be fuckin’ dead now, my friend! We just witnessed a miracle, and I want you to fuckin’ acknowledge it!”

      Vincent Vega: “Okay man, it was a miracle, can we leave now?”

      Moments later after having entered the car:

      Vincent Vega: “…ever seen that show ‘COPS’? I was watchin’ it once and this cop was on it who was talkin’ about this time he got into this gun fight with a guy in a hallway. He unloads on this guy and he doesn’t hit anything. And these guys were in a hallway. It’s a freak, but it happens.”

      Jules Winnfield: “If you wanna play blind man, then go walk with a shepherd. But me, my eyes are wide fuckin’ open.”

      Vincent Vega: “What the fuck does that mean?”

      Jules Winnfield: “That’s it for me. For here on in, you can consider my ass retired.”

      Vincent Vega: “Jesus Christ!”

      Jules Winnfield: “Don’t blaspheme!”

      Vincent Vega: “Goddammit, Jules –- “

      Jules Winnfield: “—I said don’t do that –“

      Vincent Vega: “ – you’re fuckin’ freakin’ out!”

      Jules Winnfield: “I’m tellin’ Marsellus today I’m through.”

      Vincent Vega: “While you’re at it, be sure to tell ‘im why.”

      Jules Winnfield: “Don’t worry, I will.”

      Vincent Vega: “I’ll bet ya ten thousand dollars, he laughs his ass off.”

      Jules Winnfield: “I don’t give a damn if he does.”

      Expectation: Jules Winnfield dies at the hand of the fourth man.

      Reality: Either "God came down from heaven and stopped the bullets" or it was just a "freak occurrence", but Jules Winnfield is alive and well, for the time being.


      6. So it is with us and our life. I guarantee you that you will be hit with the unexpected, and your life will never go quite as you wish it.

      If there is anything we can take away from all these examples, it is that, in the end, when it is all said and done, life never happens like you would expect it to. How long must we, in our insanity, expect the same things to produce different results? How long will we have to expect and expect and expect? How long will we have to lie to ourselves until we realize that our own agenda and our own fantasies will never play out exactly like we want them to in life? How long will it take for us to realize that this world that we are in is not about our own individual agendas and pursuits?

      There is much greater work at play here. And there is a humble invitation out there for you to get involved in this great story like you were meant to. A story about love and death and life and redemption and living for others. The alternative is, naturally, living for oneself and then dying forever. Here’s the invitation. Right here:

      Matthew 16:24-28

      "Then said Jesus unto his disciples,

      “If any man will come after me, let him deny himself, and take up his cross, and follow me. For whosoever will save his life shall lose it: and whosoever will lose his life for my sake shall find it. For what is a man profited, if he shall gain the whole world, and lose his own soul? or what shall a man give in exchange for his soul? For the Son of man shall come in the glory of his Father with his angels; and then he shall reward every man according to his works. Verily I say unto you, There be some standing here, which shall not taste of death, till they see the Son of man coming in his kingdom.”

      That's it. This world is sinking and you will too. Unless you by faith join hands with the only capable and true person in history who knows the waters that this world is sinking in, is searching for those who want to live rather than go down with the ship, and promises to take you to shore Himself. All you have to do is genuinely follow Him.


    6. There are too many "coincidences" in life for events and ourselves to be utterly random, just like how in Pulp Fiction the lives of the characters overlap at peculiar times.

      A coincidence is defined as a situation in which events happen at the same time in a way that is not planned or expected.

      List of prominent "coincidences" in Pulp Fiction:

      • Butch Coolidge comes into his apartment looking for his watch when Vincent Vega is on the toilet, able to use Vincent’s uzi to kill Mr. Vega.
      • Butch Coolidge runs into Marsellus Wallace on the way back to Fabienne as Marsellus Wallace crosses the street in front of him.
      • Vincent Vega and Jules Winnfield evade the bullets from the “goddam hand-cannon” at the hand of the fourth man.
      • The one diner that Pumpkin and Honey Bunny decide to rob, thinking it will be easy because the lack of prepared people in a restaurant, is serving prepared gangsters that end up interfering.
      • The one gun store that Butch runs into while fleeing from Marsellus, is owned and operated by two serial rapists that kidnap both Marsellus and Butch for an afternoon.

      What is key to recognize here is how a number of coincidences like the above can easily appear as mere coincidence. But what is the actual case? All of these situations were orchestrated by the author of the story - in this case, Quentin Tarantino - in order to tell a greater story, a story that utilizes the interwoven stories of the six main characters in question - Pumpkin, Honey Bunny, Mia, Butch, Vincent, and Jules - to tell a higher and fuller and more captivating and awe-inspiring narrative (in this case, the narrative has a name: Pulp Fiction).

      So it is with this world we share. The millions of coincidences that we partake in across our lifetime has such greater impact than one who believes in randomness would think. There is order to the chaos around us, and the order can only be discerned when you understand that a much greater story is being told around you, and that you have the privilege to be a part of it.

      Now this is not a perfect metaphor for how reality is to us, but it is close:

      Does Butch know that he is playing a role in a movie that was created by Quentin Tarantino? Of course not – he’s busy being Butch. Does Jules know that he is playing a role in a movie that was created by Quentin Tarantino? No, he doesn’t know the full story. But he is aware that something greater than himself saved him from those bullets. He just hasn’t realized who God is and why He stopped those bullets. Jules Winnfield doesn’t know just yet that Jules Winnfield’s god is Quentin Tarantino and Quentin stopped those bullets from hitting Jules and Vincent in the name of a greater story.

    Does the reader of these words right now know that he or she is playing a role in the great story of life that is orchestrated by the Great Composer of All Creation? That depends – either you, the reader, know the Lord and see how the Lord gives proper place, time, and opportunity to all things for His greater purpose, or you, the reader, do not know the Lord on some critical level and are busy being you. Which is fine. By all means, go and be “you”.

    But know that this world is full of evil because of our effort, by our God-given free will, to create and facilitate our own role in the movie of life rather than trust the author of all humanity to give people the best lines and the best course of action. This horrible, chaotic, evil world as we know it exists because humans do as they see fit and not as God sees fit.

    Because here’s the catch. God knows what is best for us. AND WE DON’T HAVE A CLUE, left alone to our own logic. We either trust ourselves (which is what leads to the world we are in now – an evil, ignorant, self-loathing, self-gratifying, self-seeking world), or we trust in God (which is how God intended us to live).

    Because God saw that it was good, He created man in His image, to be in relationship with Him. We are built for the company of God. It is why no amount of fame or worldly honor or glory or personal conquests achieved, we ever are truly satisfied. God knows this, and those that know Him, because of the depravity of man, know how desperately we all need Him.

    Here is a glimpse of what the future holds for those that choose to trust in God rather than themselves. I’m screamin’ at you, man. This is what comes at the end of the show. This is the third and final act:

    Revelations 21

    Then I saw “a new heaven and a new earth,” for the first heaven and the first earth had passed away, and there was no longer any sea. I saw the Holy City, the new Jerusalem, coming down out of heaven from God, prepared as a bride beautifully dressed for her husband. And I heard a loud voice from the throne saying, “Look! God’s dwelling place is now among the people, and he will dwell with them. They will be his people, and God himself will be with them and be their God. He will wipe every tear from their eyes. There will be no more death or mourning or crying or pain, for the old order of things has passed away.” He who was seated on the throne said, “I am making everything new!” Then he said, “Write this down, for these words are trustworthy and true.”

    This is the closest look at God we will ever get physically, before the death of our earthly bodies:

    Revelations 1

    I turned around to see the voice that was speaking to me. And when I turned I saw seven golden lampstands, and among the lampstands was someone like a son of man, dressed in a robe reaching down to his feet and with a golden sash around his chest. The hair on his head was white like wool, as white as snow, and his eyes were like blazing fire. His feet were like bronze glowing in a furnace, and his voice was like the sound of rushing waters. In his right hand, he held seven stars, and coming out of his mouth was a sharp, double-edged sword. His face was like the sun shining in all its brilliance. When I saw him, I fell at his feet as though dead. Then he placed his right hand on me and said: “Do not be afraid. I am the First and the Last. I am the Living One; I was dead, and now look, I am alive for ever and ever! And I hold the keys of death and Hades.”

    And here is where those who trusted in Him will dwell:

    Revelations 21

    I did not see a temple in the city, because the Lord God Almighty and the Lamb are its temple. The city does not need the sun or the moon to shine on it, for the glory of God gives it light, and the Lamb is its lamp. The nations will walk by its light, and the kings of the earth will bring their splendor into it. On no day will its gates ever be shut, for there will be no night there. The glory and honor of the nations will be brought into it. Nothing impure will ever enter it, nor will anyone who does what is shameful or deceitful, but only those whose names are written in the Lamb’s book of life.

    Us humans are apt at clinching our own fate, so I know that some part of you is wondering, if all this nonsense isn’t made-up fiction after all, how do we know whether our name is on Jesus Christ’s book of life?

    Romans 10:9

    If you declare with your mouth, “Jesus is Lord,” and believe in your heart that God raised him from the dead, you will be saved. For it is with your heart that you believe and are justified and it is with your mouth that you profess your faith and are saved.

    And of course, you know your security and identity in Christ by faith:

    Hebrews 11:1-40

    Now faith is confidence in what we hope for and assurance about what we do not see. This is what the ancients were commended for.

    By faith we understand that the universe was formed at God’s command, so that what is seen was not made out of what was visible.

    By faith Abel brought God a better offering than Cain did. By faith he was commended as righteous, when God spoke well of his offerings. And by faith Abel still speaks, even though he is dead.

    By faith Enoch was taken from this life, so that he did not experience death: “He could not be found, because God had taken him away.” For before he was taken, he was commended as one who pleased God. And without faith it is impossible to please God, because anyone who comes to him must believe that he exists and that he rewards those who earnestly seek him.

    By faith Noah, when warned about things not yet seen, in holy fear built an ark to save his family. By his faith he condemned the world and became heir of the righteousness that is in keeping with faith.

    By faith Abraham, when called to go to a place he would later receive as his inheritance, obeyed and went, even though he did not know where he was going. By faith he made his home in the promised land like a stranger in a foreign country; he lived in tents, as did Isaac and Jacob, who were heirs with him of the same promise. For he was looking forward to the city with foundations, whose architect and builder is God. And by faith even Sarah, who was past childbearing age, was enabled to bear children because she considered him faithful who had made the promise. And so from this one man, and he as good as dead, came descendants as numerous as the stars in the sky and as countless as the sand on the seashore.

    All these people were still living by faith when they died. They did not receive the things promised; they only saw them and welcomed them from a distance, admitting that they were foreigners and strangers on earth. People who say such things show that they are looking for a country of their own. If they had been thinking of the country they had left, they would have had opportunity to return. Instead, they were longing for a better country – a heavenly one. Therefore God is not ashamed to be called their God, for he has prepared a city for them.

    By faith Abraham, when God tested him, offered Isaac as a sacrifice. He who had embraced the promises was about to sacrifice his one and only son, even though God had said to him, “It is through Isaac that your offspring will be reckoned.” Abraham reasoned that God could even raise the dead, and so in a manner of speaking he did receive Isaac back from death.

    By faith Isaac blessed Jacob and Esau in regard to their future.

    By faith Jacob, when he was dying, blessed each of Joseph’s sons, and worshiped as he leaned on the top of his staff.

    By faith Joseph, when his end was near, spoke about the exodus of the Israelites from Egypt and gave instructions concerning the burial of his bones.

    By faith Moses’ parents hid him for three months after he was born, because they saw he was no ordinary child, and they were not afraid of the king’s edict.

    By faith Moses, when he had grown up, refused to be known as the son of Pharaoh’s daughter. He chose to be mistreated along with the people of God rather than to enjoy the fleeting pleasures of sin. He regarded disgrace for the sake of Christ as of greater value than the treasures of Egypt, because he was looking ahead to his reward. By faith he left Egypt, not fearing the king’s anger; he persevered because he saw him who is invisible. By faith he kept the Passover and the application of blood, so that the destroyer of the firstborn would not touch the firstborn of Israel.

    By faith the people passed through the Red Sea as on dry land; but when the Egyptians tried to do so, they were drowned.

    By faith the walls of Jericho fell, after the army had marched around them for seven days.

    By faith the prostitute Rahab, because she welcomed the spies, was not killed with those who were disobedient.

    And what more shall I say? I do not have time to tell about Gideon, Barak, Samson and Jephthah, about David and Samuel and the prophets, who through faith conquered kingdoms, administered justice, and gained what was promised; who shut the mouths of lions, quenched the fury of the flames, and escaped the edge of the sword; whose weakness was turned to strength; and who became powerful in battle and routed foreign armies. Women received back their dead, raised to life again. There were others who were tortured, refusing to be released so that they might gain an even better resurrection. Some faced jeers and flogging, and even chains and imprisonment. They were put to death by stoning; they were sawed in two; they were killed by the sword. They went about in sheepskins and goatskins, destitute, persecuted and mistreated – the world was not worthy of them. They wandered in deserts and mountains, living in caves and in holes in the ground.

    These were all commended for their faith, yet none of them received what had been promised, since God had planned something better for us so that only together with us would they be made perfect.

    You may be convinced of your own view of the world, and I totally respect that. But I'm here to tell you - there is something very unique about the love and relationship provided by Jesus Christ, there is something very special about pure and real faith in Him, and, lest your soul turn to dust in some odd 80 years, I implore you to seek Him for yourself. What you really want - deep and resilient, undying love, righteous experience, clarity and understanding, pure desires - it's all found in Him.

    And because of this truth - I'm tellin' you - you're in a 3D life-size very realistic movie, my friend, and one day the credits will roll, and you will remember that you have been sitting in a theater this entire time, and you will be confronted with hard truths like "Was I the best protagonist I could be?" and "Did I tell a good story through my actions and words and life?" and "Did I do my part in the actual movie of LIFE writ large, or was I caught up drinking from wells that will run dry and kill me of thirst in the end?"

    And there will be many who rejoice in love and many who shriek in terror when the credits roll.




    PART 4 - LUCIDITY THROUGH LIVIDITY

    "The lucidity that was to constitute his torture at the same time crowns his victory."

    - Albert Camus, The Myth of Sisyphus

    With the rage of a thousand bulls, Sisyphus starts again - up his known mountain, every step strenuous, every direction asunder.

    Here's how it happened:

    I was strolling down a garden of decaying fruit when it struck me: Only something that is eternal can be truly meaningful.

    Only that which lasts actually matters.

    I was swept up in experience and then I perceived that experience does not live on - for death comes to all that experience. And so, I asked myself, for at the end of the day, all we have is ourselves, "What matters in the end?", bearing in mind that all experience ends and therefore does not appear to matter. I perceived that what was written may matter for what is written lives on past oneself. So I scribbled for days and days, thinking to myself, I will write and write and people will know and feel what they read from me is good and true and to be listened to. Then they will see my heart for what it is, they will know the humanity within me and they will see me for who I am, not this odd robe of flesh I'm stuck in. But then I found the Book of Truth and realized everything that needed to be said had been said and nothing newly written would ever achieve the insurmountable specialness that this Book of Truth, which is the Holy Bible, held. But I decided I may as well write anyway. But, behold, after I am dead and gone, and though my words may live on a little while longer, those future people will perish and their experience will be no more. And I hated life for I saw everything is done in vain. And I perceived that I was dust and to be returned to dust and I was not needed for people perished just fine on their own without me, and I was not necessary for God like He is for Himself and His people. No, I perceived what I was - a body of dust, full of an empty spirit, pining for water to live another day so that I could be thirsty so that I may find water again to live another day so that I could be thirsty so that I could live a nice bundle of days so that I could die. I could live a nice bundle of days engineered by God, and then keel over and die and be no more. And I hated life for having death and I hated people for not seeing the reality of death and nothing made sense any more for this is the message of the wisest man of earth: All is vanity. And so I became first despondent and then livid and then despondent again at the prospect of my pointlessness.

    And my memory was squashed by the weight of the world...

    And I perceived the frailty of the human mind and the weakness of the human heart and the vanity of myself, alone, to do good. And I wanted to never have known that such evil was possible in reality, even if that meant never having been born.

    I knew not whether it was better to gasp for air in this lifeless vortex or drown in some sort of sunken sorrow...

    For I saw then how all my ways were vanity, all my efforts fruitless, and my ultimate destiny out of my control.

    I cried out in despair:

    "Oh where, oh where is the rhyme and reason

    to Chaos and Mayhem which are my seasons?"

    But, the great truth of reality drew me in like a whirlpool...

    Behold, you see, I was fast asleep, but then I woke up from my vain slumber, for my Dad had called me to check in. I said I would be at His house earlier, but I stayed asleep because it is easy and natural.

    I loathe sleeping now, knowing that I could've been awake and alive and on my way to my Father's house.

    ***

    There once was a Father and His children. They were flying high above the earth and engaged in riveting conversation. They both gazed down upon the earth, and saw the flames of sin enveloping the midst of all people.

    The Father said to His child, "All the light that you see I give to you".

    The world said, eyes brimming with fear, "Where exactly?"

    And I said, Why?

    And that has made all the difference.

    Because: You're a philosopher the moment you first ask "Why?"

    And through philosophical study, I determined:

    1. The very fact that we are motivated to do anything (that we succumb to boredom so easily) is evidence that there is some sort of meaning to life (hence, the meaning of life cannot be nothing). Motivation, whether conscious or subconscious, is purpose. And we are all motivated to accomplish certain purposes. And the right kind of purpose is truly meaningful.
    2. *
    3. If the meaning of life isn't, say, a phrase or a certain object. Then the fact that it's not that specific thing means that there is a meaning to life. If you can say "the meaning of life is not this specific object", then it follows that there is something that you can point to that is the meaning of life (even if, in your opinion, you point that meaning to nothing).
    4. *
    5. The meaning of Life is not me. So why would I make the meaning of my life about me? The meaning of my individual life ought to align with the meaning of the totality of Life, if indeed it can be done.
    6. *
    7. All spectrums of experience are stretched too far for there not to be something greater than ourselves at work in our midst. Seriously, just look around. The complexity, the simplicity, the depth, the beauty of it all. If you see nothing worth being in awe about, you're missing something. Every experience that every human being has had is bathed in divine beauty - perceiving that underlying beauty is simply a matter of the heart.

    And so it dawned on me that there must be a grand meaning of life, for:

    1. I knew that living for self-gain was curiously and totally in vain, so in order to pursue something of real merit or worth, one must pursue that something as selflessly as possible. In other words, there exists a peculiar specialness to doing selfless things and being selfless while the natural and easy thing to do is to live and act selfishly.
    2. *
    3. I knew there was a beauty that pervades all things, and I knew this beauty had to have come from somewhere. Total and complete randomness/lawlessness does not produce beauty - it produces chaos. Therefore, because there is beauty, there is at least some degree of order. For if there was no order to life, then how could any of it be beautiful?
    4. *
    5. I had tasted real, upright, undying, lasting, sincere goodness - something that could not exist on its own in an evil world that was set to be extinguished forever.

    And so I was fascinated by all things and sought to understand myself, and the human condition, and the truth of our reality in full.

    ***

    "Almost nothing important that ever happens to you happens because you engineer it. Destiny has no beeper; destiny always leans trenchcoated out of an alley with some sort of psst that you usually can't even hear because you're in such a rush to or from something important that you've tried to engineer."

    - David Foster Wallace, Infinite Jest

    I awoke and perceived some part of me had been stabbed. My heart, mightily punctured, bled its course. In the frenzy of bleeding out, I had a subconscious epiphany that I needed truth. So frantically I went through what was in front of me, confident that a syringe full of truth serum would fill my bleeding heart. I pounded on the door of the universe, demanding from the gutters of my throat, begging "Where are the truth serums? I know they are there! I demand truth! Give me truth!"

    If you didn't know the state of my heart, you'd think me an obnoxious loon.

    And lo and behold, through the eternal moments of silence that seemed to consume me, the universe did answer me.

    The universe responded to me.

    It pounded on the door of my mind, demanding from the heights of its voice, commanding, "Give me life! Give me life!"

    If you didn't know the depths of its love, you'd think the universe evil.

    And lo and behold, in exemplifying the very opposite of obnoxious evil, the universe kneeled to its knees and raised its arms up to me in proposal. And, consumed by the fire of love, the only true element of the universe, I said yes, and I gave the universe my life, and it gave me truth and all that that entails.

    And then it hit me.

    I am blessed to perceive that all life is a love story being told by the Creator to His created.

    And an abundance of other truths hit me:

    • I perceived that I could stay in the system and talk and talk and talk or dropout and actually listen to people.
    • *
    • I perceived that all men and likewise myself sought to be understood and that it was the whole duty of mine to be a voice for the misunderstood. For too many are guilty of misunderstanding what ought to be understood. And what ought to be understood is this:
      • There is no act a man can commit that does not merit my forgiveness, especially when I know that the Lord forgives all sin for those that believe in Him.
      • *
      • Love – of the true and pure and real sort - is imperative to have for all people in your life. It is imperative because of how good it is – both for the one loving and the loved ones.
      • *
      • The intrinsic beauty of the moment is total and wonderful and worthy of a righteous and praiseworthy awe.
    • I perceived that you only fear something other than God if you don't comprehend the big picture. I perceived that you only fail to love and forgive someone if you don't know God and what He did for you, and the power of His love.
    • *
    • I perceived that all those who sought abortions had been born themselves, and, behold, the voice of the unborn was unheard, squashed by the souls of the selfish. For the born sought to destroy the unborn and did not know the evil that they committed, squashing the voices of the unborn – for if the unborn could speak, I have a hunch they would scream for life.
    • *
    • *
    • I perceived that the love of wealth and materialism in America stems from a certain love for life. Although it is horrifically unfounded, currently off course and off balance in a very morbid way.
    • *
    • I perceived that all negative judgment stems from the insecurity of the judger that sees difference in the judged and, recognizing the multitude of differences between oneself and the other, in defense of what oneself is, deems the judged in a negative light to reassure themselves that what they are doing and who they are is in a positive light. For who are we to know the mind and the heart of any individual but ourselves? And this common human occurrence begs a very real philosophical question – why are we drawn to paint ourselves in this positive light, even to such a degree that we feel compelled to tarnish the light of others?
    • *
    • I perceived that all we do we do in order to have the best meal possible, the best experience within our reach, one that tastes out of this world, one that gives us the necessary fuel to accomplish whatever we set out to do, one that is shared with deeply close friends, one that is a celebration of life in its purest form. Then I knew that this meal of an experience was coming, and it had its time and place and guest list, and right now the invitation is out, but the doors will slam shut at some point, for the master of the feast knows best when and how to entertain those that have accepted his call for love and life and wonderful community.
    • *
    • I perceived that I was unfit for conventionalism.
    • *
    • I perceived that all things that are not attached to eternity pass away forever and ultimately hold no value.
    • *
    • I perceived that all people want the same thing and it is our story as a people to pursue that same thing in different ways. One way really does lead to us having that thing. All others fall short.
    • *
    • I perceived that life is meant to be lived to the fullest and that there are many forces at play actively working to stop you from living life the way it is meant to be lived.
    • *
    • I perceived that even perception is fallible, like our hearts.
    • *
    • I perceived that
      fantasy
      is the
      truth
      of this
      dream
      • Define: Fantasy = the reality of imagination.
      • Define: Imagination = the brain's freedom.
      • Define: Freedom = anything you choose to describe it
        • Therefore, the reality of the brain's choice is the truth of this dream. In other words, your reality will match however you choose to perceive reality, but pray that however you choose to perceive reality accurately correlates to
          objective reality

    And it was like, though the thunder roared around me and the rain poured ceaselessly, all I could see were these flashes of brilliance, these aphorisms of lightning, this internal clarity despite blatant external confusion. And this is what I saw:

    • We are here to be taught to trust God over ourselves. Because of sin, we trust the life that we make for ourselves instead of what is infinitely better, the life that God provides for us.
    • *
    • Man is a little less evil when he stops gazing down with arrogance at the inadequacy of others and starts staring up with wonder at the beauty of the inadequacy of others and shouts with glee, "Truly you are superior! And at the very least, my equal!"
    • *
    • The biggest mistake in history was disobeying God. The biggest mistake we currently make is disobeying God.
    • *
    • "Sex is what dogs do on the side of the street. The intimacy and love and connection I have with my wife when we make love cannot be called that." Sin seeks to convince you of the lie that indulging in sin is living life to the full when the true tragedy is that it is robbing you of that fullness. Fullness is lived God's way.
    • *
    • I perceived that all human desire ends with emotional stimulus. Based on my experience and faith, I know God is what we all desire. We are meant to engage in relationship with God. And so we all strive for emotional stimulus that is, reflects, or is close to God. We all long for praise, no matter where it comes from. We all long to satisfy and act on things that lead to who we want to be. But that glory is selfish. And in the most humbling paradox of all, abandoning selfish aspirations will lead you to exactly what you thought those selfish aspirations would accomplish – life, love, success, wealth, health, fullness – whatever it is you truly desire - it is found in Jesus Christ and all given to you by Him according to His good will.
    • *
    • There are two paths. One is accepting the grace of Jesus Christ and realizing that you will never be good enough on your own and that you need God to be good. The other is that you worship some other idol that lies to you and claims that if you work or do or be a certain way, then you are good enough or that you will then be satisfied. One is the path of truth and God. The other is the path of lies and the self. How long will it take each of us to realize that on our own we go nowhere and do no good thing? You either live for God or you live for yourself. One of those will lead to life. The other death.
    • *
    • This is the life that Jesus yearns to give us: a life consumed by beautiful livelihood, fullness of love, and betterment of self.
    ***

    I am imperfect and have sinned many times. In truth, I do not know people like my Father - like not even close - and therefore it is imperative that I refrain from judgment upon all others, and espouse love, like my Father has said. But in loving the Father, we inevitably come to follow His commandments.

    And so with love in mind, consider these:

    • Just like scientific theories are models that have not been thwarted by experimentation, so too does the literature of the bible stand up to my reality. And of course, inevitably, surpasses so much more.
    • *
    • Sure, the message of novels can be summed up to be a sentence or two. But hearing a sentence doesn’t even scrape the surface of understanding that your mind can handle. A novel allows the message to not just be severely unknown, but allows it to soak in the mind, leading to knowing the true weight of that slender sentence summary. The same rule applies to why we live a lifetime and not a moment. It's simply better to learn from a lifetime than a moment.
    • *
    • The meaning of anything is whatever the creator of that something wants it to be. Yes, interpreters are free to interpret. But that does not change the original and authoritative intention of the created piece.
    • *
    • It's like I woke up from a trance, excited to realize that I had been performing on a stage for a nonexistent audience, and eager to step off stage to a truer reality. Humbled by my awakening, I yearned to call back to my colleagues on stage and scream at them the truth: "You're acting!!! You're performing!!! Can't you see that you have given yourself into some vain game that has sought to control your mind and tragically succeeded? What are you seeking when you do well at the games in your head?" But, alas, no words could reach them, for uncovered fears roamed the caverns of their mind and held tight to the reigns of their will, convincing them to play a false role on a fake stage, despite truth being in them and around them, mere steps away. Saddened by the blindness of the world, I exited stage left and hurried home to true love.
    • *
    • Life is like a roller coaster. And we can see the roller coasters of others. I am turning my attention away from the roller coasters of others and focusing on my own ride. And only then will I be able to fully enjoy it!
    • *
    • And I dreamt that some generation would come from the shadows and save us and sanctify us but behold no one came because no one knows, no, not one, but Him.
